Jamison Brereton

15 (456)
Agni
V─лtahavya ─Ас╣Еgirasa or Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
19 verses: jagat─л 1тАУ2, ┼Ыakvar─л 3, jagat─л 4тАУ5, ati┼Ыakvar─л 6, jagat─л 7тАУ9, triс╣гс╣нubh 10тАУ14, ┼Ыakvar─л 15, triс╣гс╣нubh 16, anuс╣гс╣нubh 17, brhati 18, tri ╠е с╣гс╣нubh 19, arranged in trcas ╠е
With its nineteen verses, this hymn as a unity would clearly be out of place in the arrangement of the maс╣Зс╕Нala, but dissolved into a series of five independent tr╠еcas, its first fifteen verses fit well. The last four verses (16тАУ19) are considered by Oldenberg (1888: 194) to be a later addition, and their vocabulary shows certain signs of com
parative modernity. The content of these triads is generally unremarkable, concentrating on the installation of the ritual fire, AgniтАЩs sacrificial role as envoy between gods and men, and the ritual service performed for him by mortals. To some extent the tr╠еcas seem to be exercises in variation; for example, the first verses of the first two tr╠еcas (1, 4) share some key words and phrases and can in part be interpreted by compari
son with each other.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPropitiate by praises this guest who wakes at dawn, the cherisher of all people, who on every occasion descends, pure of origin, from heaven, and, present as the embryo (in the wood of attrition), consumes immediately the offered (oblation).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This guest of yours here, waking at dawn, lord of all clans will I stretch toward with my hymn.
He, ablaze right from his birth, pursues any (food) whatever
from heaven here. For a long time the embryo eats just what is
immovable.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On с╣Ы├▒jase see comm. ad IV.8.1. A tr. тАЬaim at/towardsтАЭ would be more transparent here.

The problematic p─Бda here is c: div├бс╕е, k├бc cid, and ─Б╠Бare difficult to construe and interpret. Geldner takes the first as referring to тАШdayтАЩ rather than тАШheavenтАЩ and makes it dependent on k├бc cid: тАЬzu jeglicher Zeit des Tages,тАЭ but div├бс╕е is far more often тАШheavenтАЩ than тАШdayтАЩ (the latter sense usually confined to use with tr├нr ─Б╠Бand a few temporal adverbs). Renou takes div├бс╕е as an abl. of тАШheavenтАЩ (тАЬIl sтАЩavance du cielтАЭ), and he takes the k├бc cid adverbially with j├бnuс╣г─Б тАж ┼Ы├║ciс╕е (тАЬpur de toute mani├иre quant ├а la naissance,тАЭ where the indefinite sense of k├бc cid has been replaced by a totalizing one). In the published translation I agree with Renou in taking div├бс╕е as ablative of тАШheavenтАЩ, construing it with distant ─Б╠Б, and supply тАШfoodтАЩ with k├бc cid. But I now donтАЩt think this makes much sense. I will suggest an alternative that makes more sense, but that doesnтАЩt solve all the difficulties and requires some special pleading.

First IтАЩd observe that the word order in this p─Бda seems particularly contorted.

I ascribe this to the position of jan├║с╣г─Б: this instr. occurs 20 times in the RV and it always occurs immediately after the caesura, whatever its function in the clause. In this particular case, it is generally agreed that jan├║с╣г─Б should be construed with ┼Ы├║ciс╕е (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 1c), despite the intervening material. IтАЩd argue that the need to plunk down jan├║с╣г─Б smack in the middle of the p─Бda has disrupted the constituencies of the rest of the p─Бda as well. Therefore, we cannot use word order and adjacency as reliable guides here (even less so than in the rest of the RV).

Now, letтАЩs start with the verb v├йti, which opens the p─Бda, and with the observation that the poet of this hymn is supposed to be V─лtahavya, who is in fact mentioned in both the other vss. of the tс╣Ыca (2c, 3d). If we decompose this cmpd.

name we can make a putative havy├бm тАШoblationтАЩ the object of v├йti (cf. I.74.4 v├йс╣гi havy─Б╠Бni; sim. III.53.1, VI.60.15, etc.; for similar gapping in this hymn, see 14b), which can be qualified by k├бc cid: тАЬhe pursues any (oblation) whatever.тАЭ I further suggest that div├бс╕е should be construed with ─Б╠Б, as in my published interpr., but that here ─Б╠Б means тАШall the way to XтАЩ, rather than тАШfrom X hereтАЩ. Although in the тАШall the way toтАЩ sense, ─Б╠Бnormally precedes the ablative (see Grassmann, s.v. ─Б╠Б), as already noted, the word order in this p─Бda seems particularly scrambled, and, in any case, ─Б╠Бoften follows an acc. in the тАШtoтАЩ sense. I would therefore now substitute the tr. тАЬJust he, blazing from birth, pursues any oblation whatever all the way to heaven.тАЭ This would be a description of the flames rising up towards heaven as they carry the oblation up to the gods.

The next p─Бda is implicitly contrastive: although the flames of the ritual fire actively reach for heaven in p─Бda c, the fire itself, just kindled, starts by burning the kindling sticks, which are immovable as opposed to the oblation later poured into the fire.

The cadence of d is bad.

Griffith

WITH this my song I strive to reach this guest of yours, who wakes at early morn, the Lord of all the tribes.
Each time he comes from heaven, the Pure One from of old: from ancient days the Child eats everlasting food.

Diesem eurem fr├╝hwachen Gast, dem F├╝rsten aller St├дmme will ich fein mit meiner Lobrede den Vorzug geben. Zu jeglicher Zeit des Tages verlangt er nach Speise, rein schon bei der Geburt. Seit langer Zeit verzehrt der Neugeborene selbst das was fest ist.

Mit meinem Liede streb’ ich diesem euren Gast, der Morgens wacht, dem Herren aller St├дmme zu; Vom Himmel dringt nach seiner Art auf alles hin der lichte Spross, verzehrt, was fest ist, lange schon.

рд╡рдирд╕реНрдкрддреМ рдЕрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдзрд┐рддрдВ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдореН рдИрдбреНрдпрдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрдореН рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рд╢реЛрдЪрд┐рд╖рдореН рдЙрдЪреНрдЫреНрд░рд┐рддрддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрдХрдВ рдпрдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рди рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдорд┐рд╡ рд╕рдЦрд┐рднреВрддрдорд┐рд╡ рднреГрдЧрд╡рдГ рдорд╣рд░реНрд╖рдпрдГ рджрдзреБрдГ рдЖрджрдзреБрдГ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ, рд╣реЗ рдЕрджреНрднреБрдд рдорд╣рдиреНрдирдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╕рдГ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдГ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡реАрддрд╣рд╡реНрдпреЗ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮ рдЛрд╖реМ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░реАрддрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдкреНрд░реАрдпрдорд╛рдгреЛ рднрд╡ ред рдпрддрдГ рджрд┐рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд╡реЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреИрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реИрдГ рдорд╣рдпрд╕реЗ рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрд╕реЗ ред рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬ рдЛрд╖рд┐рд╢реНрдЪреЗрддреН рд╡реАрддрд╣рд╡реНрдпреЗ рджрддреНрддрд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдХреЗ рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬ рдЗрддрд┐ рдпреЛрдЬрдиреАрдпрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWonderful Agni, whom, adorable and upward flaming, the bhс╣Ыgus regard as a friend, deposited in the wood of (attrition), be plural ased with v─лtahavya, since you are glorified by (his) praise everyday.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

V─лtahavya: if applied to bharadv─Бja, it will be an appellation, he by whom oblations are offered

Jamison Brereton

Whom the Bhr╠еgus installed like a well-installed envoy, to be reverently invoked at the тАЬtreeтАЭ [=sacrificial post], with flames erect,
you, o infallible one, well pleased in V─лtahavya, are magnified with
eulogies every day.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich treats Agni in the accusative, so that no grammatical person needs to be expressed. It therefore appears to continue the 3rd ps. of vs. 1, but modulates to the 2nd ps. reference of cd.

Griffith

Whom, well-dis sed, the Bhrgus stablished as a friend, whom men must glorify, high-flaming in the wood.
As such, most friendly, thou art every day extolled in lauds by Vitahavya, O thou wondrous God.

Geldner

Den die Bhrigu┬┤s wie einen Freund gut aufnahmen, den im Holze Wohlaufgehobenen, Anzurufenden mit aufgerichteten Flammen, du wirst wohlbefriedigt bei Vitahavya, du Geheimnisvoller, mit Lobreden Tag f├╝r Tag gefeiert.

Grassmann

Den wohlbewahrt die Bhrigu’s bargen in dem Holz, wie einen Freund, den herrlichen, hochflammenden, Erfreut wirst du bei Vitahavja, himmlischer, durch Preisges├дnge, vielgeliebter, Tag f├╝r Tag.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрджреНрднреБрдд ! рдпрдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рди рд╕реБрдзрд┐рддрдВ рд╡рдирд╕реНрдкрддрд╛рд╡реАрдбреНрдпрдореВрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рд╢реЛрдЪрд┐рд╖рдВ рднреГрдЧрд╡реЛ рджрдзреБрдГ рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрджрд┐рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд╡реЗ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░реАрддрдГ рд╕рдиреН рд╡реАрддрд╣рд╡реНрдпреЗ рдорд╣рдпрд╕реЗ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрд╕реЗрд╡рдиреАрдпреЛрд╜рд╕рд┐ реереирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдореН) рд╕рдЦрд╛рдпрдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдпрдореН) (рд╕реБрдзрд┐рддрдореН) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдореН (рднреГрдЧрд╡рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рджрдзреБрдГ) рджрдзрддрд┐ (рд╡рдирд╕реНрдкрддреМ) рд╡рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпреЗ (рдИрдбреНрдпрдореН) рдЙрддреНрддрдореИрд░реНрдЧреБрдгреИрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрдореН (рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рд╢реЛрдЪрд┐рд╖рдореН) рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рдореН (рд╕рдГ) (рддреНрд╡рдореН) (рд╕реБрдкреНрд░реАрддрдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрдирдГ (рд╡реАрддрд╣рд╡реНрдпреЗ) рд╡реАрддрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╣реАрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ рдпреЗрди рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН (рдЕрджреНрднреБрдд) рдорд╣рд╛рд╢рдпред рдЕрджреНрднреБрддрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдорд╣рдиреНрдирд╛рдоред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрей.рей) (рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдзрд░реНрдореНрдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рдорд╣рдпрд╕реЗ) рд╕рддреНрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╕реЗ (рджрд┐рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд╡реЗ) рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рдирдореН реереирее

03 рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдореН - рд╢рдХреНрд╡рд░реА

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDo you, who are unresisted, become the benefactor of him who is skilled (in sacred rites), his defender against a near of distant enemy; son of strength, who are ever renowned, grant wealth and a dwelling to v─лtahavya, the offerer of the oblation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

V─лtahavya, the bearer, bharat, of the oblation;

V─Бja = bharadv─Бja, by whom is offered, v─лta, the oblation, havya

Jamison Brereton

YouтАФbecome a strengthener of our skill, one who keeps the wolf away, an overcomer of the stranger, distant or close.
O son of strength, (hold out) riches among mortals, hold out shelter of great extent to V─лtahavya, of great extent to Bharadv─Бja.

Griffith

Be thou the foeless helper of the skilful man, subduer of the enemy near or far away.
Bestow a wealthy home on men, O Son of Strength. Give Vitahavya riches spreading far and wide, give Bharadvaja wide-spread wealth.

Geldner

Sei du ein sicherer F├╢rderer des T├╝chtigen, ein ├Ьberwinder des fremden und des nahen Nebenbuhlers. Verleih, o Sohn der Kraft, unter den Sterblichen dem Vitahavya Reicht├╝mer und deinen Schirm in ganzer Breite, dem Bhagradvaja deinen Schirm in ganzer Breite.

Grassmann

Sei du des T├╝cht’gen treugesinnter F├╢rderer, des nahen und des fernen Feinds Bew├дltiger; Und Sch├дtze gib, o Sohn der Kraft, den Sterblichen; dem Vitahavja reiche ausgedehnten Schutz, (dem Bharadvadscha weiten Schutz.)

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPropitiate with pious praises the radiant Agni, your guest, the guide to heaven, the invoker of the gods( at the sacrifice) of manu, the celebrator of holy rites, the speaker of brilliant words like a learned sage, the bearer of oblations (to the gods), the lord, the divine.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your flashing guest with his solar glory, Agni, the Hotar conducting good ceremonies for Manu,
possessing heaven-ruling speech like an inspired poet, the
oblation-conveying spoked wheel (of the sacrifice)тАФto (this) god
I stretch with my well-twisted (hymns).

Griffith

Him, your refulgent guest, Agni who comes from heaven, the Herald of mankind, well-skilled in sacred rites,
Who, like a holy singer, utters heavenly words, oblation-bearer, envoy, God, I seek with hymns.

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН ! рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡реЛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдорддрд┐рдерд┐рдорд┐рд╡ рджреНрдпреБрддрд╛рдирдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдгрд░рдВ рдордиреБрд╖реЛ рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдзреНрд╡рд░рдордЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рд╕реБрд╡реГрдХреНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрди рджреНрдпреБрдХреНрд╖рд╡рдЪрд╕рдВ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╛рд╣рдорд░рддрд┐рдВ рджреЗрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рди рдЛрдЮреНрдЬрд╕реЗ рддрдВ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕рддреНрдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдо реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджреНрдпреБрддрд╛рдирдореН) рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерджреНрдпреЛрддрдХрдореН (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рдореН) рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рдорд┐рд╡ (рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдгрд░рдореН) рдпрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдГ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдирдпрддрд┐ рддрдореН (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрдореН (рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдореН) рдЖрджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдореН (рдордиреБрд╖рдГ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрдп (рд╕реНрд╡рдзреНрд╡рд░рдореН) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареНрд╡рдзреНрд╡рд░рд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрддрдореН (рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореН) рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рджреНрдпреБрдХреНрд╖рд╡рдЪрд╕рдореН) рджреНрдпреЛрддрдХрд╡рдЪрдирд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдХрдореН (рд╕реБрд╡реГрдХреНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рднрд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рд╣рд┐рддрдореН (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╛рд╣рдореН) рдзрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╛рд╣рдХрдореН (рдЕрд░рддрд┐рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХрдореН (рджреЗрд╡рдореН) рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдЛрдЮреНрдЬрд╕реЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдиреЛрд╖рд┐ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Propitiate him) who shines upon the earth with purifying and enlightening lustre, as the dawns with ligt; him, who like (a warrior) discomfiting (his foes) quickly blazed forth in the contest in defence of eta┼Ыa; him, who is satiated (with food), exempt from decay.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In defence of eta┼Ыa;

Eta┼Ыa = a horse?

Jamison Brereton

Who with his pure, conspicuous body shines on earth as if with the radiance of Dawn,
who goes in triumph on his course now like the victor in the battle with Eta┼Ыa [=the sunтАЩs horse], who is athirst (for oblations?) here, like (a
traveler) in the (sunтАЩs) heat, the unaging oneтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b both Geldner and Renou take uс╣г├бsaс╕е as a nom. pl. rather than a gen. sg. as I do (e.g., тАЬcommes les aurores avec leur rayonтАЭ). Either would work contextually.

However, in IV.1.17 in the phrase uс╣г├бso bh─Бn├║с╕е (like our uс╣г├бso n├б bh─Бn├║n─Б), uс╣г├бsaс╕е has to be gen. sg. and Geldner so interprets it there.

In c and d I take the crucial terms with double reference, in both simile and frame. In c this term is the pres. part. t┼л╠Бrvan: in the frame it refers to Agni and is construed with loc. y─Б╠Бman тАЬgoing in triumph on his courseтАЭ; in the simile it is construed with loc. r├бс╣Зe тАЬlike the victor in the battle.тАЭ The battle with (lit. of) Eta┼Ыa is a reference to the conflict between Indra and the Sun involving the SunтАЩs horse Eta┼Ыa in some unfortunately puzzling way. To make this clear, тАЬbattle over Eta┼Ыa would be a better rendering, as Michael Weiss points out to me. A further resonance of this phrase t┼л╠Бrvan n├б y─Б╠Бman is the PN T┼лrvay─Бс╣Зa found several times in the RV, incl.

nearby VI.18.13.

n┼л╠Бin c seems to have no function and is curiously positioned, though it might be noted that there’s a minority position of n├║/n┼л╠Б, penultimate in the p─Бda, and this is fairly common in VI.

As for d, the standard interpr. (Oldenberg ZDMG 313 + Noten, Geldner, Renou) take the part.

tatс╣Ыс╣г─Бn├бс╕е only with the simile; this requires supplying an elaborate verbal predicate (тАЬgoes to waterтАЭ) that is not found in the Sanskrit; cf., e.g., Oldenberg тАЬer der herbei (eilt) wie im Sonnenbrand der Durstende (zum Wasser eilt).тАЭ I again think that the participle applies in both simile and frame: in the simile it refers to someone becoming thirsty in the (sunтАЩs) heat, whereas in the frame it refers to Agni тАЬthirstingтАЭ for oblations. This participle is used unambiguously of Agni elsewhere (I.31.7, II.4.6) in describing his voracious appetite for fuel.

In a clever poetic trick the sun is referred to indirectly in both c (his horse Eta┼Ыa) and d (his heat: ghс╣Ыс╣З├б-).

Griffith

Who with his purifying, eye-attracting form hath shone upon the earth as with the light of Dawn;
Who speeding on, as in the fight of Etaia, cometh, untouched by age, as one athirst in heat.

Geldner

Der in reiner, ausgezeichneter Sch├╢nheit auf Erden erstrahlt wie die Usas in ihrem Glanz, der den Vorsprung gewinnt in der Fahrt wie der Sieger in der Wettfahrt, wie im Kampfe des Etasa, der herbei eilt wie der Durstige in der Sonnenglut, der Alterlose.

Grassmann

Der auf der Erde strahlt wie mit des Morgens Glanz, mit seiner hellen, leuchtend flammenden Gestalt, Im Wettlauf vordringt auf des Sonnenrosses Bahn, der ewige junge, der nicht d├╝rstet in der Glut.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWorship repeatedly the adorable Agni with fuel (him) who is ever your dear friend, your guest; approach the immortal Agni with praises, for he, a god among gods, accepts our homage.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To your every fire do friendly service with a kindling stick, to your every dear guest in hymning (them).
Seek to win the immortal one with your hymns, for the god will win what is choice among the gods; for the god will win friendship for us among the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The locatival inf. gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бс╣Зi occurs only here and in VIII.12.19. Curiously, in both passages it is construed with ─Бmreс╕Нitas: here priy├бm-priyam тАж ├бtithim (matching agn├нm-agnim in p─Бda a), in VIII.12.19 dev├бс╣Г-devam тАж ├нndram-indram. I donтАЩt quite know what to do with this fact. Keydana (p. 178) takes it as a тАЬMatrixinfinitivтАЭ functionally equivalent to an imperative, pointing to impv.

duvasyata in p─Бda a. However, it would also be possible to interpret it as I do, with duvasyata the main verb of both p─Бdas and the infinitive an adverbial adjunct to both p─Бdas. I would change the tr. of the ─Бmreс╕Нitas, however, to one more in harmony with that in VIII.12.19: тАЬTime after time do friendly service to the fire with a kindling stick, time after time to your dear guest, in hymning (him).тАЭ The morphology of gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бс╣Зi is of course unusual, though it belong with the small group of RV -san-i locatival infinitives, some of which (cf. esp. upastс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бс╣Зi, which, however, I now consider to be based on gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бс╣Зi; see comm. ad VI.44.6) are built to already derived verbal stems (see AiG II.2.924-25). In this passage it phonologically echoes ghс╣Ыс╣З├й and tatс╣Ыс╣г─Бс╣З├бс╕е in the preceding vs. (5d), and in the next vs. (which also belongs to the next tс╣Ыca) p─Бda-final gс╣Ыс╣Зe, which is also of course etymologically related.

Griffith

Worship ye Agni, Agni, with your log of wood; praise your beloved, your beloved guest with songs.
Invite ye the Immortal hither with your hymns. A God among the Gods, he loveth what is choice, loveth our service, God mid Gods.

Geldner

Immer huldiget eurem Agni mit Brennholz, immer feiert euren lieben Gast; machet mit Lobreden den Unsterblichen euch geneigt, denn der Gott gewinnt von den G├╢ttern alles W├╝nschenswerte, denn der Gott gewinnt bei den G├╢ttern Achtung.

Grassmann

Beschenkt den Agni stets mit eurem Flammenholz, und preiset hoch ihn euren lieben, lieben Gast; Gewinnet euch durch Lieder den Unsterblichen; denn zu den G├╢ttern bringt der Gott die Sch├дtze hin; (denn zu den G├╢ttern bringt er unsre Gaben hin.)

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI glorify with praise the kindled Agni, pure purifying, permanent, (plural ced) before (us) at the sacrifice; let us celebrate with plural asant (hymns) the wise Agni, the invoker of the gods, the adored of many, the benevolent, the far-seeing, him who knows all that exists.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni kindled with kindling wood do I hymn with a hymnтАФthe blazing pure one in front, steadfast at the ceremony,
inspired poet, Hotar of many favors, without deceitтАФthe sage poet we beseech with appeals for grace as J─Бtavedas.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. begins a new tс╣Ыca, but seems like a mish-mash of the vss. that precede it. The 1st p─Бda, s├бmiddham agn├нс╣Г sam├нdh─Б gir─Б╠Бgс╣Ыс╣Зe, telescopes vs. 6: agn├нm-agnim тАж sam├нdh─Б (a), gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бс╣Зi (b), g─л╠Бrbhiс╕е (c). It also contains two etymological figures (s├бmiddham тАж sam├нdh─Б and gir─Б╠Бgс╣Ыс╣Зe). The next p─Бda, ┼Ы├║cim p─Бvak├бm pur├│ adhvar├й dhruv├бm, is more eclectic in its sources: ┼Ы├║ciс╕е (1c), p─Бvak├бy─Б (5a), svadhvar├бm (4b); p─Бda-final dhruv├бm has no direct correspondent, but resonates with both d├║vaс╕е (p─Бda-final in 6e) and adr├║ham, which ends the next p─Бda (7c). The first two words of p─Бda c, v├нpraс╣Г h├│t─Бram have correspondents in 4c and b respectively. Only p─Бda d breaks significantly new ground.

Griffith

Agni inflamed with fuel in my song I sing, pure, Cleanser, steadlast, set in tront at sacrifice.
Wise Jatavedas we implore with prayers for bliss the Priest, the holy Singer, bounteous, void of guile.

Geldner

Den mit Brennholz entflammten Agni lobe ich mit Lobrede, den reinen, lauteren mache ich dauernd zum Vorsitzer bei dem Opfer; den beredten Opferpriester, den vielbegehrten, untr├╝glichen Seher, den Jatavedas bitten wir mit freundlichen Worten.

Grassmann

Ich preis’ mit Lied den Agni, der durch Holz entflammt, hell vor dem Opfer aufgerichtet, brennend steht; Den sch├дtzereichen, holden S├дnger, Opferer und Wesenkenner flehn mit Lied, den weisen, wir.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, have gods and men in every age retained as their messenger, immortal bearer of oblations, beneficent, adorable; they have plural ced him with reverence (upon the altar), vigilant, pervading, the protector of mankind.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, have they established in every generation as immortal messenger, as oblation-conveyor, as protector to be reverently invoked.

Both gods and mortals set down with homage the wakeful one as their far-extending clanlord.

Griffith

Men, Agni, in each age have made thee, Deathiess One, their envoy, offering-bearer, guard adorable.
With reverence Gods and mortals have established thee, the ever-watchful, omnipresent Household Lord.

Geldner

Dich, den Unsterblichen, o Agni, machten sie in jedem Zeitalter zum Boten, zum Opferfahrer, den anzurufenden Sch├╝tzer. G├╢tter und Sterbliche setzten den Wachsamen als ihren m├дchtigen Stammesf├╝rsten unter Verbeugung ein.

Grassmann

Als Boten setzten, Agni, dich unsterblichen, als Opferfahrer, werthen H├╝ter, allezeit Die G├╢tter und die Menschen ein, den wachenden, den starken F├╝rsten setzten hin sie ehrfurchtsvoll.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShowing grace, Agni, to both (gods and men), and at each sacred rite the messenger of the gods, you traverse earth and heaven; inasmuch as we offer you worship and praise, therefore do you, who are the guardian of the three (regions), be auspicious to us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Seeking manifestation, o Agni, following the commandments of both (men and gods) you speed between the two airy realms altogether. Since we choose for ourselves your thought as grace, so become a kindly provider of threefold defense for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation fails to tr. d┼лt├│ dev─Б╠Бn─Бm. The tr. should be emended to тАЬтАж as messenger of the gods, you speed тАжтАЭ The lexeme v├н тИЪbh┼лс╣г occurs only here and I.112.4 until Epic, and it is not entirely clear what it means here. тАЬSeeking manifestationтАЭ of the published translation depends on the usage of rare v├н тИЪbh┼л, which can mean тАШbecome manifestтАЩ; an example is found (at least by my lights) in vs. 14. But it might have the less marked meaning тАШbecoming conspicuous, distinguishedтАЩ or тАШbecoming extended/extensiveтАЩ. In any case it picks up vibh├║m, which opens the last p─Бda of the preceding vs. Note also the polarized preverbs v├н and s├бm at opposite ends of the hemistich.

The Pp. takes ubh├бy─Бm╠Рas acc. pl. masc. ubh├бy─Бn (so also Grassmann), but as Oldenberg suggests (ZDMG 55.313, Noten), it could be neut. pl. ubh├бy─Б with nasalization in hiatus, and a neut. pl. construed with vrat─Б╠Бis an attractive choice here. The phrase ubh├бy─Б(m) ╠Р ├бnu vrat─Б╠БтАЬfollowing both (kinds of) commandmentsтАЭ would of course refer to those of gods and men, who were mentioned in 8c.

Griffith

Thou, Agni, ordering the works and ways of both, as envoy of the Gods traversest both the worlds.
When we lay claim to thy regard and gracious fare, be thou to us a thriceprotecting friendly guard.

Geldner

Beide Teile nach den Geboten in Ordnung haltend suchst du, Agni, als Bote der G├╢tter beide Welten auf. Wenn wir deine Aufmerksamkeit und Gunst erbitten, so sei uns dreifach sch├╝tzend, freundlich!

Grassmann

Die beiden St├дmme, Agni, schm├╝ckend nach der Pflicht, besuchst als G├╢tterbote beide Welten du; Wenn deine Gunst, dein freundlich Sorgen wir erflehn, so sei du heilvoll, sei du dreifach schirmend uns.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe of little wisdom adore the most wise Agni, the well-formed, the well-looking the graceful-moving; may Agni, who knows all things that are to be known offer the sacrifice; may he announce the oblation to the immortals.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Him, of lovely countenance, of lovely appearance, of lovely outlook, might we, who do not know, serve as the one who knows better. He will perform sacrifice, knowing all the patterns; Agni will proclaim our oblation among the immortals.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is rhetorically pleasing, though unremarkable in content. It opens with three cmpds with su- as first member, all in the realm of appearance (at least as I interpret the sequence) supr├бt─лkaс╣Г suс╕Нс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыaс╣Г s(u)v├б├▒cam. The next p─Бda juxtaposes a negated form of the pf. part. of тИЪvid with a comparative built to the same stem (though different allomorph), ├бvidv─Бс╣Гso vid├║с╣гс╣нaram, picked up by a third form to this participle, vidv─Б╠Бn, at the end of the next p─Бda – which itself participates in an alliterative sequence v├н┼Ыv─Б vay├║n─Бni vidv─Б╠Бn.

sv├а├▒c- of course patterns and inflects with the -a├▒c- stems, generally built to preverbs/adverbs in the meaning of тАШdirectedтАЩ (e.g., ├║da├▒c- тАШdirected upwardтАЩ), and in 2 of its 6 occurrences (IV.6.9, VII.56.16) the context favors the sense тАШwelldirectedтАЩ (VI.58.4 is unclear). But here, as well as in similar adjectival sequences in VII.10.3 and in IX.73.7, it appears with words referring to seeing or appearance, and I suggest that this usage preserves a semantic relic of the тАШeyeтАЩ word (*h3eku╠п ) that, according to most, is one contributor to the blend that produces the hybrid suffix - a├▒c- (see, e.g., AiG III.230). I therefore render it in these contexts as тАШof lovely outlookтАЩ (contra GeldnerтАЩs тАШsch├╢n von тАж BewegungтАЩ). RenouтАЩs тАШde belle allureтАЩ avoids the directional sense and may reflect an analysis similar to mine, but he does not comment. A zero-grade of the тАШeyeтАЩ word is also buried in pr├бt─лka-, also found in our sequence (supr├бt─лka-), and in ├бn─лka, which contributes svan─лka- in 16a (for both see EWA s.vv.).

Although p─Бda-final vidv─Б╠Бn is generally used absolutely, here it must take an object, vay├║n─Бni.

The clear s-aor. subj. yakс╣гat in c invites a subjunctive reading of vocat in the next p─Бda, though it is of course injunctive. Nonetheless, modal readings are quite common for this stem.

Griffith

Him fair of face, rapid, and fair to look on, him very wise may we who know not follow.
Let him who knows all rules invite for worship, Agru announce our offering to the Immortals.

Geldner

Ihn, der sch├╢n von Erscheinung, von Anblick und Bewegung, wollen wir Unkundige den Kundigeren in Ehren halten. Er soll opfern, der alle Wege kennt, Agni soll den Unsterblichen das Opfer ansagen.

Grassmann

Der sch├╢n von Antlitz, lieblich und gewandt ist, den weisen lasst uns th├╢richte verehren; Er, jedes Kunstwerk kennend, m├╢ge opfern, den G├╢ttern Agni unser Opfer k├╝nden.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддрдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдВ рдкрд╛рд╕рд┐ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╕рд┐ ред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рддрдВ рдкрд┐рдкрд░реНрд╖рд┐ рдХрд╛рдореИрдГ рдкреВрд░рдпрд╕рд┐ ред рдпрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛ рд╣реЗ рд╢реВрд░ рд╢реМрд░реНрдпрд╡рдиреНрдирдЧреНрдиреЗ рдХрд╡рдпреЗ рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рдп рддреЗ рддреБрднреНрдпрдВ рддреНрд╡рджрд░реНрдердВ рдзреАрддрд┐рдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЖрдирдЯреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред тАШ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдордгрдГ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирддреНрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереА ред рдХрд╡рд┐рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдзреАрддрд┐рдорд╛рдирдЯреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ ред рддрдВ рдкрд╛рд╕реАрддреНрдпрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рдпрд╛рдЧрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рддрддреНрд╕рд╛рдзрдирднреВрддрд╕реНрдп рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реЛ рд╡рд╛ рдирд┐рд╢рд┐рддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд╛ редрдирд┐рд╢рд┐рддрд┐рдГ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рддрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЙрджрд┐рддрд┐рдореН рдЙрджреНрдЧрдордирдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЖрдирдЯреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ рддрдорд┐рддреН рддрдореЗрд╡ рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛ рдмрд▓реЗрди рдкреГрдгрдХреНрд╖рд┐ рдкреВрд░рдпрд╕рд┐ ред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд░рд╛рдпрд╛ рдзрдиреЗрди рдкреВрд░рдпрд╕рд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou cherish, you protect, Agni, that may who offers worship, hero, to you, the far-seeing; you reward with strength and with riches him (who undertakes) the instrumental tution, (who effects) the accomplishments of the sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who effects: ya├▒asya v─Б ni┼Ыitim v─Б uditim v─Б: saс╣Гsk─Бra, perfection, accomplishment; udgamanam, going up or over, perhaps, finishing

Jamison Brereton

Him, o Agni, do you protect and him do you rescue, who has achieved an insightful thought for you, the sage poet, o champion,
or (who has achieved) the тАЬwhettingтАЭ of the sacrifice, or its (proper) outcome. Just him do you imbue with power and with wealth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is unusually conjunction-heavy, with ut├б in p─Бda a (conjoining clauses) and in d (conjoining nouns), and v─Б 3x in c. In fact there at first appear to be more v─БтАЩs than there are constituents to conjoin: yaj├▒├бsya v─Б n├н┼Ыitiс╣Г v─Б-├║ditiс╣Г v─Б.

However, Klein (DGRV II.195) plausibly explains the first v─Б as sentential (I would prefer the term тАШclausalтАЩ in this case), connecting p─Бda b with its relative clause y├бс╕е …

─Б╠Бnaс╣н тАж with its continuation in p─Бda c. The other two v─БтАЩs are subclausal, conjoining the two -ti-stem action noun phrases, n├н┼Ыitiс╣Г v─Б-├║ditiс╣Г v─Б, both of which govern the gen. yaj├▒├бsya, the constituency being interrupted by the clausal v─Б in WackernagelтАЩs position.

In c I assume that the verb is a gapped repetition of ─Б╠Бnaс╣н. Klein tr. the skeleton of bc as тАЬwho has attained тАж or (has brought about) тАж,тАЭ so I assume he thinks c has a different underlying verb from b. But the full VP n├н┼Ыitim тАж ─Б╠Бnaс╣н in nearby VI.13.4, as well as VI.2.5 n├н┼Ыitim тАж na┼Ыat also in this Agni cycle, establish this as a ritual idiom.

Note the complementary preverbs n├н тАШdownтАЩ and ├║d тАШupтАЩ in the conjoined n├н┼Ыitim тАж ├║ditim. The latter word is not otherwise used as a ritual term; in all its other occurrences it is a loc. and refers to the rising of the sun. Here it seems to refer to the outcome or the progress of the sacrifice, though it could be more narrowly used for the тАЬrising upтАЭ of the fire when it is kindled. This is probably the better interpr. because in 2 of the 4 occurrences of n├н┼Ыiti-, VI.2.5 and VIII.19.14, it is implicitly use of the fire.

Griffith

Him, Agni, thou deliverest and savest who brings him prayer to thee the Wise, O Hero,
The end of sacrifice or its inception; yea, thou endowest him with power and riches.

Geldner

Agni! Du sch├╝tzest und f├╝hrest den aus der Not, der dir, dem Seher, o Held, eine Dichtung fertig gebracht hat oder den Anreiz oder guten Ausgang des Opfers, den erf├╝llst du mit Macht und Reichtum.

Grassmann

Den schirmst du Agni, sicher ihn geleitend, wer dir, dem Seher, Andacht weiht, o starker; Des Opfers Anbruch oder Schluss herbeif├╝hrt, den auch erf├╝llst mit Kraft du und mit Reichthum.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬProtect us, Agni, from the malignant, preserve us, mighty one, from wickedness; may the offering come to you free from defects; may desirable riches, by your sands, (reach us).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, AgniтАФprotect (us) from the rapacious one, and you, mighty oneтАФ (protect) us from reproach.
Let the smoke-enwrapped (oblation) come entirely to you, to the fold (of the gods); let thousandfold desirable wealth (come)
entirely.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The problematic p─Бda here is c. The initial s├бm in both c and d and the fact that d otherwise contains only a phrase in the nominative invite us to assume that c and d have the same structure and that we should supply the verb abhy ├иtu from c for d, as well as, quite possibly, tv─Б. But though the NP in d, тАЬthousandfold desirable wealth,тАЭ is something we would quite naturally invite to тАЬcome to you entirely,тАЭ the general assumption is that dhvasmanv├бt, whether it modifies p─Б╠Бthaс╕е тАШfoldтАЩ (Grassmann, Renou) or not (Oldenberg, Geldner), refers to something undesirable – e.g., OldenbergтАЩs (ZDMG 55.313) tentative тАЬwas voll von Zerfall [decay] ist.тАЭ It is therefore uncomfortable to invite it to come anywhere near Agni or us. Certainly both occurrences of its base dhvasm├бn- (IV.6.6, VIII.66.15) are in fact in negative contexts. But the substance itself, smoke, is semantically neutral, and in this ritual context something тАШpossessing smokeтАЩ can be positive: the oblation as it is poured into the fire will be surrounded by smoke, and, by one model of the sacrifice, it will go to the gods in AgniтАЩs smoke as that smoke rises to heaven. I therefore supply havy├бm here (found in this tс╣Ыca in 10d), and take tv─Б and p─Б╠Бthaс╕е as two sequential accusatives of goal. Agni is the first destination of the smoke-wrapped oblation, which must be poured into the fire, but it then goes to тАЬthe fold (of the gods)тАЭ for their consumption – dev─Б╠Бn─Бm is a standard dependent gen. with p─Б╠Бthaс╕е (esp. in ─Аpr─л hymns, II.3.9, III.8.9, etc.).

Griffith

Guard us from him who would assail us, Agni; preserve us, O thou Victor, from dishonour.
Here let the place of darkening come upon thee: may wealth be ours, desirable in thousands.

Geldner

Sch├╝tze du, Agni, vor dem Neider, du uns vor Tadel, du Gewaltiger! Alles, was einen Beschmutzer hat, soll insgesamt bei dir Zuflucht finden, bei dir kommt begehrenswerter, tausendf├дltiger Reichtum zusammen.

Grassmann

Du schirm uns, Agni, vor dem h├дndels├╝cht’gen und vor Verleumdung uns, o kraftbegabter; Es dring mit dir dein rauchumh├╝llter Gang vor und tausendfacher, vielbegehrter Reichthum.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, is the invoker of the gods, the lord of the house, the ruler, who knows all that is, knows all existing beings; he is the mos assiduous worshipper among gods or men; let him who is observant of truth offer worship.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni is the Hotar, the houselord; he is the king. He knows all the creatures, as J─Бtavedas.
He who is of gods and of mortals the best sacrificer, let him, the truthful one, set the sacrifice in motion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b is nicely configured: v├н┼Ыv─Б veda j├бnim─Б j─Бt├бved─Бс╕е. The first two and the last two words alliterate. The final word, the epithet j─Бt├бvedas-, is immediately preceded by two independent words etymologically related to its two members (in reverse order): veda to -ved─Бс╕е, j├бnim─Б to j─Бt├б-. (Of course, -vedas- may ultimately derive from тИЪvid тАШfind, possessтАЩ, but at least folk-etymologically it belongs with тИЪvid тАШknowтАЩ.) And v├н┼Ыv─Б veda evokes the cmpd vi┼Ыv├б-vedas-, a parallel formation to j─Бt├бvedas-. Nothing profound here, but a pleasing way to deploy four words.

Griffith

Agni, the Priest, is King, Lord of the homestead, he, Jatayedas, knows all generations.
Most skilful worshipper mid Gods and mortals, may he begin the sacrifice, the Holy.

Agni ist der Hotri, der Hausherr, er der K├╢nig. Als Jatavedas kennt er alle Geschlechter; der unter G├╢ttern und Menschen der beste Opferer ist, er soll ordungsgem├д├Я opfern.

Grassmann

Agni ist Priester, Hausgebieter, K├╢nig; der Wesenkenner kennet alle Wesen; Der unter G├╢ttern, und der unter Menschen am besten opfert, opfre nun, der heil’ge.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, minister of the sacrifice, bright wiht purifying lustre, approve of that (worship) which is this day celebrated by the instrumental tutor of the rite; you verily are the sacrificer, therefore address the worship (to the gods); and since by your greatness you are all-pervading, therefore, youngest (of the gods), accept the oblations which are today (presented) to you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Agni, pure-flamed Hotar of the ceremony, when today you pursue (the oblations) of the clanтАФfor you are the sacrificerтАФ
you will offer true (hymns?) as sacrifice when you have become manifest in your greatness. O youngest one, convey the oblations that are yours today.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda is a 13-syllable Triс╣гс╣нubh; as Oldenberg notes (ZDMG 55.313 and Noten), it would be possible to delete init. ├бgne without affecting sense, but on the other hand it is difficult to see why it would have been secondarily appended.

In p─Бda a it is unclear how to construe vi┼Ы├бс╕е. Note first that by accent it must be abl./gen. sg., not acc. pl. (v├н┼Ыaс╕е). Geldner (see n. 14ab) takes it as a second gen. with following voc. hotaс╕е, but in that case we would expect vi┼Ы├бс╕е to lose its accent in the voc. phrase (as adhvaryasya has), and, further, vi┼Ы├│ h├│tar- is not a standard title, as far as I can find. It might be possible to supply *p├бti- тАЬ(lord) of the clan,тАЭ matching gс╣Ыh├бpatiс╕е in the previous vs. (13a), next to h├│t─Б; cf. vi┼Ыp├бtiс╕е in 8d. However, I think the most likely solution is similar to the one also proposed for 1c – to supply havy├бm as the object of v├йс╕е in b (see havy─Б╠Бin d), with vi┼Ы├бс╕е dependent on havy├бm. Recall that the poetтАЩs name is V─лtahavya, and he seems to like concealed puns on his name.

As a support for their connection, note that the two phonologically similar words vi┼Ы├бс╕е and v├йс╣г take the same position in their respective p─Бdas. RenouтАЩs solution is somewhat similar to mine, with vi┼Ы├бс╕е dependent on an object supplied for v├йс╕е, but his proposed object is тАЬla fonction du messagerтАЭ and he makes adhvarasya a parallel gen. to vi┼Ы├бс╕е ignoring its lack of accent. His supplied obj. d┼лty─Б╠Аni is certainly conceivable: he adduces IV.7.8 v├йr adhvar├бsya d┼лty─Б╠Аni тАж But to my mind the pun on the name of the poet weighs more heavily.

In p─Бda b there is close sandhi in the sequence v├йс╣г с╣н(u)v├бm; the reason for this is unclear, esp. since by all standard interpr. (incl. mine) t(u)v├бm belongs to a new clause – the parenthetical one marked by h├н – and so there is a particularly sharp syntactic boundary between them.

In c mahin─Б╠Бfits semantically much better in the subordinate y├бd clause than in the main clause (and is so taken by the standard interpr.), but it seems to be positioned too far to the left, with another element interposed before the subordinator: тАж mahin─Б╠Бv├н y├бd bh┼л╠Бс╕е. I attribute this word order disturbance to the same factor that caused trouble in 1c: like jan├║с╣г─Б, mahin─Б╠Бonly occurs immediately after the caesura in trimeter vs. Given this constraint, the only possible adjustment to produce the expected sequence would be an ordering mahin─Б╠Б*y├бd v├н, which would put the subordinator in the correct 2nd position of its clause but produce a bad Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence (- - тПС ├Ч). A somewhat similar situation is found in II.1.15c pс╣Ыkс╣г├│ y├бd ├бtra mahin─Б╠Бv├н te bh├║vat, where mahin─Б╠Бcauses some distortion in word order, though the placement of the subordinator is not affected.

With L├╝ders (438) I take с╣Ыt─Б╠Бas neut. acc. pl. and supply тАШhymnsтАЩ (Lieder), rather than taking it as an instr. sg.; this interpr. is supported by VII.39.1 с╣Ыt├бm тАж yaj─Бti, with the neut. sg. acc. Note the phonetic interplay of v, h, and y in d havy─Б╠Бvaha yaviс╣гс╣нha y─Б╠БтАж

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLook, Agni, upon the (sacrificial) viands duly deposited (upon the altar); heaven and earth detain you to sacrifice (to the gods); opulent Agni, protect us in battle, whereby we may pass safe over all evils; may we pass over those of a prior existence; may we pass over them by your protection.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you watch over the well-placed pleasurable offerings then. One should set you down, to sacrifice to the two world-halves.
Help us, bounteous one, in the winning of prizes. Agni, may we cross over all (narrow straits) difficult to traverse; may we cross over
themтАФwith your help may we cross over.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Oldenberg points out (see published introduction.), this is no doubt the last vs. of this collection of tс╣Ыcas, with vss. 16-19 later additions. There is some faint sign of ring composition with the first tс╣Ыca: s├║dhit─Бni in p─Бda a reprises s├║dhitam in 2a, as dadh─лta with Agni as object does dadh├║с╕е also in 2a. The last three p─Бdas of this vs., esp. de, appear to be a refrain: p─Бda e is identical to VI.2.11e = 14.6e in this Agni cycle, and p─Бda d ├бgne v├н┼Ыv─Бni durit─Б╠Бtarema is a variant of VI.2.11d = 14.6d dviс╣г├│ ├бс╣Гh─Бс╣Гsi durit─Б╠Бtarema, hence my supplied тАЬnarrow straitsтАЭ here. These refrain p─Бdas also signal that the hymn (or the tс╣Ыcas loosely collected into a hymn) once ended here.

On the anomalous position of h├н here, see comm. ad III.31.12, where the idiosyncratic behavior of тИЪkhy─Б is discussed. Here the immediate preverbal position of h├н is esp. anomalous because the preverb abh├н has been fronted (as opposed to III.31.12 тАж v├н h├н ky├бn #, where the preverb stays in the verb complex).

Griffith

Look thou upon the viands duly laid for thee. Fain would he set thee here to worship Heaven and,Earth.
Help us, O liberal Agni, in the strife for spoil, so that we may o’ercome all things that trouble us, o’ercome, o’ercome them with thy help.

Geldner

So betrachte denn die wohlbereiteten Opfergen├╝sse. Der Priester soll dich einsetzen, um beiden Welten zu opfern. Sei uns g├╝nstig bei der Lohngewinnung, o Gabenreicher! O Agni, ├╝ber alle F├дhrlichkeiten m├╢chten wir hinwegkommen, wir m├╢chten ├╝ber diese hinwegkommen, durch deine Gnade hinwegkommen.

Grassmann

So sieh dir an die wohlgesetzten Speisen; dich w├дhlt man gern zu opfern beiden Welten; Uns hilf, o m├дcht’ger, bei der Opferspende, lass, Agni, alles Ungl├╝ck uns durchschreiten; (kraft deiner Gunst lass du hindurch uns schreiten.)

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBright-rayed Agni, sit down first with all the gods, upon the altar lined with wool, a nest (of perfumes) and suffused with ghee, and rightly convey (to the deities) the sacrifice of the instrumental tutor of the rite, of the presenter of the oblation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Lined with wool: urс╣З─Бvantam, kul─Бyinam ghс╣Ыtavantam; the с╣Ыca is quoted in Aitareya Br─Бhman.a; the altar is bult up like the nest of a brid, kulaya, with circles, padhayaс╕е, of the wood of the khayar or devad─Бru, in which aviс╣гambandaс╕е romavi┼Ыeс╣гaс╕е, sheep’s wool; and fragran resins, the materials of incense (guggulu dhup─Бt dhanam) are plural ced, ete uttaravedy─Бm sth─Бpitaс╕е, these appurtenances are plural ced in the northern altar. Of the protector of oblation: savitre yajam─Бn─Бya = (in genitive tive case) с╣гaс╣гс╣нyarthe caturthyeс╣гa; anuс╣гс╣н─Бtre yajam─Бn─Бya tadupak─Бr─Бrtham, for the sake of the benefit of the sacrificing instrumental tutor of the ceremony

Jamison Brereton

O Agni of the lovely face, with all the gods sit first on the
woolly womb,
the ghee-rich one that forms a nest. Lead the sacrifice straight, for the impeller (of the sacrificer), for the sacrificer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase тАЬwooly wombтАЭ (┼л╠Бrс╣З─Бvantam y├│nim) is striking as a designation of AgniтАЩs seat. Geldner (n. 16b) thinks it refers to the barhis, but in fact the fire is not placed on that dry grass, which might produce a conflagration disruptive to the ritual.

I think it must rather refer to twigs and foliage still present on the firewood. In agreement with Geldner (who is hesitant – see n. 16c) and Renou, I see a verseinternal enjambment: the two accusatives directly after the hemistich boundary, kul─Бy├нnaс╣Г ghс╣Ыt├бvantam, qualify y├│nim, which ends p─Бda b; then there is a syntactic break in the middle of the p─Бda, with dat. savitr├й construed with d, not c. This is unusual, but it is difficult to find a function for savitr├й in the preceding clause.

Griffith

Together with all Gods, O fair-faced Agni, be seated first upon the woollined altar,
Nest-like, bedewed with oil. Bear this our worship to Savitar who sacrifices rightly.

Geldner

Sch├╢ngesichtiger Agni! Mit allen G├╢ttern setze dich als erster auf den wolligen Scho├Я, den nestartigen, schmalzreichen! Zu Savitri geleite das Opfer richtig f├╝r den Opfernden.

Grassmann

O Agni, mit allen G├╢ttern setze dich, o sch├╢ner, zuerst in den wollenweichen Schooss hin, in den fettbegabten, der einem Neste gleicht; das Opfer f├╝hre auf rechtem Wege dem opfernden Antreiber.

Elizarenkova

рд╡реЗрдзрд╕рдГ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рддрд╛рд░ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ рдЗрдордВ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рддреНрдпрдВ рддрдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрдЧреБрдгрдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН рдЕрдерд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН рдпрдерд╛рдерд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЦреНрдп рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдордереНрдирд╛рддреН рддрдерд╛ рдордиреНрдердиреНрддрд┐ рдордереНрдирдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрд░рдгреНрдпреЛрдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рдЬреНрдЬрдирдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдЩреНрдХреВрдпрдиреНрддрдореН ред рдХреБрддреНрд╕рд┐рддрдордЮреНрдЪрдирдВ рдЧрдордирдореН рдЕрдЩреНрдХреБред рддрджрд╛рддреНрдорди рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдВ рджреЗрд╡реЗрднреНрдпреЛ рдирд┐рд░реНрдЧрддреНрдпреЗрддрд╕реНрддрддрдГ рдкрд▓рд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирдореН рдЕрдореВрд░рдореН рдЕрдореВрдврдВ рдпрдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рднреНрдпрдГ ред рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡реАрддрд┐ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдирд╛рдо ред рддрддреНрд░ рднрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрддрдорд╕рдГ рд╕рдВрд╣рддрдпрдГ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рддрд╛рднреНрдпрдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рдЖрдирдпрдиреН рдЖрдЧрдордпрдиреН рддрдВ рдордиреНрдердиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe priests churn you, Agni, as was done by atharvan, and bring him from the glooms of night wandering deviously, but not bewildered.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Wandering deviously, but not bewildered: aс╣Еkuyantam amuram: the reference is to a legent of Agni’s attempting at first to run away from the gods, devebhyaс╕е p─Бlayam─Бnam

Jamison Brereton

This Agni here the ritual adepts churn, as Atharvan (did)тАФ (Agni) who, (though) he sought a crooked (path), they led here unerring from the dark (places).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou take aс╣Еk┼лy├бnt- as a positive quality parallel to ├бm┼лra-; e.g., Renou: тАЬ(dieu) faiseur de m├йandres, (dieu) exempt dтАЩegarement.тАЭ I think rather that they are opposites and that the vs. concerns the flight of Agni and his recovery by the gods: note the imperfect ─Б╠Бnayan (Pp. ─Б╠Б├бnayan, though technically it could be ─Б╠Бnayan with an injunctive). Though Agni sought to elude the gods by taking a circuitous course, they found him and brought him straight back from the dark depths of the water. The тАЬdark placesтАЭ can of course also refer to the night, after which the ritual fire is kindled, but I think the primary reference is mythological.

Griffith

Here the arranging priests, as did Atharvan, rub this Agni forth,
Whom, not bewildered, as he moved in winding ways, they brought from gloom.

Geldner

Diesen Agni reiben die Meister wie Atharvan heraus, den sie aus dem Dunkel herf├╝hrten, den Schleichwege Gehenden, nie Irrenden.

Grassmann

Hier diesen Agni reiben nach Atharvan’s Art die Ordner hervor, den in Windungen gehenden, weisen, den sie hervorf├╝hrten aus der Dunkelheit.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рддрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд╕реНрддрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдиреЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдордереНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬрдирд┐рд╖реНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рджреБрд░реНрднрд╡ ред рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердореН ред рджреЗрд╡рд╡реАрддрдпреЗ рджреЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдп рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп ред рд╖рд╖реНрдареНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛ ред рдИрджреГрд╢рд╕реНрдп рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрдпреЗ рдЕрд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рд╛рд░реНрдердореН ред рдЬрдирд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЪ рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рдиреН рдорд░рдгрд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдиреН рдЛрддрд╛рд╡реГрдзрдГ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддреДрдиреН рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЖ рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐ рдЖрд╡рд╣ ред рддрджрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рддреЗрд╖реБ рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рдкрд┐рд╕реНрдкреГрд╢рдГ рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢рдп ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBe born, Agni, at the sacrifice, for the welfare of the offerer (of oblation) to the gods; bring hither the immortal deities, the augmenters of the (sacred) rite present our sacrifice to the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Be born, to pursue the gods in their entirety, for well-being. Convey the gods hither, the immortals growing strong through truth. You cause the sacrifice to touch the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On j├бniс╣гv─Б as belonging to the -iс╣г-aorist, see Narten (Sig.-Aor, 68).

Griffith

For the Gods’ banquet be thou born, for full perfection and for weal.
Bring the Immortal Gods who strengthen holy Law: so let our sacrifice reach the Gods.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLord of the house, Agni, we, among men, promote your increase by soma or fuel; may our domestic fires be supplied with all that is essential; enliven us with brilliant radiance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With all that is essential: asth┼лri = asth┼лriс╣Зa g─Бrhapaty─Бni santu; isth┼лri is properly a one-horse car or waggon which bring either the soma or fuel; with negative prefix asth┼лri, it implies a non-one-horse cart, that is a cart with a full team, and metonymically, its contents, or a full supply of what is wanted for a perfect sacrifice, such as children, cattle, riches, asth┼лriс╣Зi putra-pa┼Ыu-dhan─Бdibhiс╕е saс╣Гp┼лrс╣З─Бni

Jamison Brereton

O Agni, houselord of the people(s), we have made you lofty with kindling wood.
May our household (arrangements) not be тАЬone-horse.тАЭ With your
sharp sharpness hone us thoroughly.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The slangy asth┼лr├н тАШnot one-horseтАЩ is appropriate to this later addition to the hymn. Its positive sth┼л╠Бri тАШone-horseтАЩ is found in the RV only once in the late X.131.3.

Griffith

O Agni, Lord and Master of men’s homesteads, with kindled fuel we have made thee mighty.
Let not our household gear be found defective. Sharpen us with thy penetrating splendour.

Geldner

Wir haben dich, du Hausherr der Menschen, Agni, mach uns scharf mit schneidiger Kraft!

Grassmann

Wir haben dich, o Agni, Hausherr der Menschen, gross gemacht durch Brennholz; vielspannig sei auch unsre Hausherrschaft, o sch├дrfe uns mit heisser Flammensch├дrfe.

Elizarenkova

рдкреБрдирд░реНрдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдереИрдГ рдХрдердВ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рдпрдореН) (рдЙ) (рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН (рдЧреГрд╣рдкрддреЗ) рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ (рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рджреНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рдЕрдХрд░реНрдореНрдо) рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдо (рд╕рдорд┐рдзрд╛) рдкреНрд░рджреАрдкрдХреЗрди рд╕рд╛рдзрдиреЗрди (рдмреГрд╣рдиреНрддрдореН) рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрдереВрд░рд┐) рдЕрд╕реНрдерд┐рд░рдВ рдпрд╛рдирдореН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдЧрд╛рд░реНрд╣рдкрддреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐) рдЧреГрд╣рдкрддрд┐рдирд╛ рд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдореНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ (рд╕рдиреНрддреБ) (рддрд┐рдЧреНрдореЗрди) рддреАрд╡реНрд░реЗрдг (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛) (рд╕рдореН) (рд╢рд┐рд╢рд╛рдзрд┐) рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреНрддрдпрд╛ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдп реерезрепрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдерд╛ рдЬрдирд╛ ! рдпреВрдпрдорд╛рд▓рд╕реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдп рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЛрдиреНрдирддрд┐рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рдиреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рдпрдд рдпреЗрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд░реНрдзреЗрд░рдиреНрдирд┐рддрд┐ реерезрепрее рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдердХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрдГ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рдкреНрд░рдердореЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдерд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рдЖрд│рд╕ рд╕реЛрдбреВрди рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХреНрд░рдорд╛рдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗрдЪреА рдЙрдиреНрдирддреА рдХрд░рд╛. рдЗрддрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рд╡рд╛. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рд╡рд╛рдвреЗрд▓. рее резреп рее
